            The single most serious foundational problem is this:
                                                                                (n, l, m)

            is being used in three incompatible ways: Fourier exponent, Lorentzian BKM root
            degree, and would-be physical/Hall charge degree. The first two are additive. The third
            is generally not additive if (n, l, m) are Gram invariants of physical charges.
            That has to be fixed before any compact Hall/factorization story can be more than a
            recognition wish-list.

            1. Fatal issue: Gram invariants are not physical Hall charges

            extension-closed Hall category with numerical Gram-index lattice Γind , semistable
            stacks indexed by γ ∈ Γind , and Hall correspondences landing in γ + η.

            8. The Ran(E) obstruction is good, but phrase it narrowly
            Your observation is correct: if a one-dimensional subscheme C ⊂ K3 × E has
            positive elliptic degree, then pE (C) = E . Therefore such a curve cannot be localized at
            finitely many points of E . The manuscript uses this to argue that naive support-local
                                                             ​




            factorization on Ran(E) sees only projection-finite sectors.
                    raeez.lorgat.automorphic-correc…

            That is one of the strongest original conceptual points in the draft.
            But do not overstate it as a general obstruction to locality. It is an obstruction to a
            particular pushforward-to-Ran(E) model. A six-dimensional local theory on K3 × E
            can still have local observables; the problem is that positive elliptic-degree curve
            sectors are global from the E -projection viewpoint.
            Required repair
            Replace “locality obstruction” with:
               projection-to-E support-locality obstruction.
            That avoids a physicist objecting that you are confusing spacetime locality with support-
            locality after dimensional reduction.

            9. The BKM denominator is not a microscopic BPS algebra

            The denominator algebra is real mathematics: Gritsenko–Nikulin construct a generalized

                                                                                                                                 ​




            Cartan matrix with entries 2 on the diagonal and −2 off the diagonal. arXiv
                                                             ​




            But the BKM algebra is not automatically the algebra of BPS states. You already know
            this and state it. The determinant only fixes signed supermultiplicities:
                                                     smult(α) = dim gα,0 − dim gα,1 .  ​                     ​




            It does not fix the two dimensions separately, invisible zero-superdimension root

            Take any graded super vector space B with
                                                                 sdim Bn,l,m = f (nm, l)

            and give it the zero bracket. It has the same determinant, but it is not gΔ . Your own
            Proposition 10.31 says the determinant forgets brackets, parity splits, simple-root

            representatives, relation constants, and Hopf-pairing radicals.

            12. Boundary rows: good ledger, but too much row-map danger
            The Cléry–Gritsenko result really is an eight-row classification of genus-two Siegel

            Siegel forms are precisely the dd-modular forms classified by Cléry–Gritsenko and arise
            as Weyl–Kac–Borcherds denominators. arXiv
            So your ledger is defensible. But this part is high-risk because you are mixing:
                Cléry–Gritsenko row order,
                your row order,
                CHL GN (M ) notation,
                product-degree lattices,
                                   ​




                multiplier covers,
                scalar squares,
                denominator identities,
                physical hosts.
            A hostile reader will search for one row-map mismatch and use it to discredit the
            appendix.

            The pair c = (Q, P ) is primitive saturated, or torsion-one, if
                                                              Mc = Λ ∩ (Mc ⊗ Q).

            Equivalently, in a coordinate basis this is the condition usually written

            The original DVV Igusa-counting formula is the torsion-one dyon formula; torsion > 1
            dyons require extra discrete data beyond Q2, P 2, Q ⋅ P . arXiv +1
            Now use the lattice theorem.
            For an even unimodular indefinite lattice Λ with enough hyperbolic planes, primitive
            embeddings of a fixed even rank-two lattice M are unique up to O(Λ) once the
            complement has sufficiently large rank relative to the discriminant length. The standard
            Nikulin criterion gives uniqueness when the positive and negative signatures have room
            and
                                                          rk(Λ) − rk(M ) ≥ 2 + ℓ(AM ),               ​




            where AM = M ∨ /M is the discriminant group. For rank-two M , ℓ(AM ) ≤ 2, while
            H (S , Z) has rank 24 and Γ6,22 has rank 28, so the condition is overwhelmingly
                             ​                                                                             ​




            satisfied away from the usual boundary degeneracies. math.brown.edu
            Thus, for primitive saturated pairs,
                           O(Λ)\{(Q, P ) ∈ Λ2 : Π(Q, P ) = (n, l, m), gcd(Q ∧ P ) = 1}                         ​




            is a single orbit, subject to the standard signature and chamber conditions.

            10. The physics interpretation
            The two Künneth Mukai components
                                               Q = (0, −β, −k),                          P = (1, 0, 1 − d)

            are the two physical charge vectors whose Gram invariants are counted by the Igusa
            variables.
            The K3 curve norm gives
                                                                       Q2 /2 = h − 1.

            The D0/Fourier charge gives
                                                                             Q ⋅ P = k.

            The elliptic degree, with the Todd/vacuum shift, gives
                                                                       P 2 /2 = d − 1.

            So the Igusa triple is physically
                                                   Q2         P2
                                      (n, l, m) = ( , Q ⋅ P ,    ) = (h − 1, k, d − 1).
                                                   2          2
                                                                   ​                 ​                        ​

                                                               ∏ (1 − q n rl sm )f (nm,l) .
                                                                         ​




                                                             (n,l,m)>0

            The product does not live directly on the raw physical lattice. It lives on the primitive
            Gram quotient of the physical lattice.
            That is the construction.

            Thought for 6m 51s
            Yes. The paper should be Dirac-inspired in exactly this sense:
               Do not begin with a scalar partition function and ask for a square root.
               Begin with a first-order physical object whose scalar shadow is a square.
            That is the Dirac move. Dirac did not take an analytic square root of the Klein–Gordon
            operator. He introduced new algebraic degrees of freedom — spinors and Clifford
            multiplication — such that the square became scalar. Your paper should do the same.
            The Igusa square root should not be presented as a branch of Δ25. It should be
            presented as the first-order protected chiral/Pfaffian object whose scalar reduced
                                                                                                       ​




            DT/OP theory is the square. Your current manuscript already gestures at this through
            protected locality, the E3-source, the orientation character, and the statement that the
            scalar square forgets the automorphic reflection sign. The rewrite should make that the
                                                    ​

            1. States are not first. Observables are first.
28/04/2026, 09:03                                                    Attack Whitepaper Analysis




            A charged BPS state is not a local field. It is a sector. Its charge is measured at infinity.
            Therefore the microscopic Hilbert space is not the natural first object.
            The first object is the algebra of protected operations.
            A state is a representation of that algebra. A partition function is a trace of that
            representation. A trace cannot reconstruct the algebra. So the paper should not begin
            with the scalar trace and then apologize that it cannot reconstruct locality. It should
            begin with locality and then show what trace it produces.
            The physical hierarchy should be:
             local protected operations ⟶ factorization/Hall algebra ⟶ primitive Lie algebra

            This is already latent in your manuscript, but it should become the philosophical and
            technical backbone.

            2. The physical charge lattice
            Let
                                                              X = S × E,

            where S is a K3 surface.
            The even Mukai lattice of S is
                                    ΛS = H (S, Z) = H 0 (S, Z) ⊕ H 2 (S, Z) ⊕ H 4 (S, Z),

            with pairing
                                             (r, D, s) ⋅ (r′ , D′ , s′ ) = D ⋅ D′ − rs′ − r′ s.

            Since
                                               H even (X, Z) ≅ H (S, Z) ⊗ H even (E, Z),

            every even charge decomposes as
                                                  vX (F ) = P (F ) ⊗ 1E + Q(F ) ⊗ ωE .
                                                       ​                  ​                       ​

            3. The local object on X
            The local object is not the scalar DT series. The local object is the protected open-string
            observable algebra on the Calabi–Yau threefold X .
            In the B-model language, the local field theory on a Calabi–Yau threefold is holomorphic
            Chern–Simons/BV theory. Locally, for a brane background F , the fields are controlled by
            the dg Lie algebra

            or, perturbatively,
                                                                       Ω0,∗

            classical interaction is cubic:

                                                                2      3

            The compact nonperturbative version replaces one fixed brane by the derived stack of
            compactly supported branes.
            For an open U ⊂ X , let

            be the derived stack of compactly supported coherent B-branes in U with physical
            charge

            6. Locality fails exactly where it should fail
            Now the important point: positive elliptic degree is not local on E .
            Let C ⊂ S × E be a one-dimensional subscheme with positive elliptic degree:
                                                                (pE )∗ [C] = d[E],
                                                                      ​    ​                                           d > 0.

            Then pE (C) is a one-dimensional closed subset of the irreducible curve E . Hence
                         ​




                                                                                       pE (C) = E.
                                                                                           ​




            Therefore C cannot be assigned to finitely many points of E .
            This is not a mathematical inconvenience. It is the physics.
            A brane wrapping E is not a local insertion on E . It is a global sector, just as a Wilson
            loop is not a pointlike local observable in the direction it wraps. It can couple to local
            insertions, but it is not itself localized at their points.
            Therefore the correct object is not simply
                                                                               Fact(Ran(E)).

            9. Unitarity is used before the index, not after it
            The paper should be very explicit here.
            The untwisted theory is unitary. This matters because it gives an adjoint supercharge:
                                                                    Q† ,

            and an identity of the form
                                                             {Q, Q† } = Hright .      ​




            Then all states with positive right-moving energy pair and cancel in the protected
            supertrace. This is why the K3 elliptic genus localizes.
            So unitarity supplies the cancellation theorem.
            But after taking Q-cohomology, one no longer has a positive Hilbert space. One has a
            cohomological, charge-graded, virtual object.
            Thus
                                                                  f (n, l)

            is a superdimension, not a dimension.
            A negative coefficient means an odd excess:
                                           f (n, l) < 0       ⟺       dim H1ˉ − dim H0ˉ > 0
                                                                                  ​                    ​




            in whatever protected representative realizes it.
            The Borcherds denominator algebra is also not a unitary Hilbert-space representation.
            Its Cartan lattice is Lorentzian. Its multiplicities are signed supermultiplicities:
                                                     smult(α) = dim gα,0ˉ − dim gα,1ˉ .
                                                                             ​                     ​




            This is exactly what one expects from a protected cohomological theory.
            So the correct statement is:

             unitarity is an input to localization;                             the square root is a cohomological protected

            That is not a weakness. It is the nature of an index.

            11. The denominator algebra as the first-order equation

            3. The cocycle theorem
            For
                                                       c = (Q, P ),            c′ = (Q′ , P ′ ),

            define
                                     B(c, c′ ) = (Q ⋅ Q′ , Q ⋅ P ′ + Q′ ⋅ P , P ⋅ P ′ ) ∈ Γind .             ​   ​




            This is the polarization of the quadratic Gram map.
            Theorem 3.1 — B is a symmetric bilinear normalized 2-cocycle
            For all c, c′ , c′′ ∈ Γphys
                                   X ,          ​




                                                              B(c, c′ ) = B(c′ , c),

                                                    B(c + c′ , c′′ ) = B(c, c′′ ) + B(c′ , c′′ ),

                                                    B(c, c′ + c′′ ) = B(c, c′ ) + B(c, c′′ ),

            and
                                                             B(c, 0) = B(0, c) = 0.

            Moreover,
                                                    Π(c + c′ ) = Π(c) + Π(c′ ) + B(c, c′ ).              ​




            Consequently B satisfies the additive 2-cocycle equation
                                     B(c, c′ ) + B(c + c′ , c′′ ) = B(c′ , c′′ ) + B(c, c′ + c′′ ).                  ​




            Proof
https://chatgpt.com/c/69efa55c-63c4-83ea-b3fc-fc3666b5910f                                                               47/220
28/04/2026, 09:03                                                               Attack Whitepaper Analysis

            Write c = (Q, P ), c′ = (Q′ , P ′ ), c′′ = (Q′′, P ′′). Symmetry is immediate from
            symmetry of the lattice pairing.
            Bilinearity follows because each component of B is bilinear in (Q, P ) and (Q′ , P ′ ). For
            example,
                                                   (Q + Q′ ) ⋅ Q′′ = Q ⋅ Q′′ + Q′ ⋅ Q′′ ,

            and similarly for the other components.
            The Gram-defect identity follows from expanding:
                                                    (Q + Q′ )2   Q2   Q′2
                                                               =    +     + Q ⋅ Q′ ,
                                                        2        2     2
                                                                   ​            ​                 ​




                               (Q + Q′ ) ⋅ (P + P ′ ) = Q ⋅ P + Q′ ⋅ P ′ + Q ⋅ P ′ + Q′ ⋅ P ,

                                                    (P + P ′ )2   P2   P ′2
                                                                =    +      + P ⋅ P ′.
                                                        2         2     2
                                                                   ​            ​                 ​




            Thus
                                                 Π(c + c′ ) = Π(c) + Π(c′ ) + B(c, c′ ).

            Finally,
                               B(c, c′ ) + B(c + c′ , c′′ ) = B(c, c′ ) + B(c, c′′ ) + B(c′ , c′′ ),

            while
                              B(c′ , c′′ ) + B(c, c′ + c′′ ) = B(c′ , c′′ ) + B(c, c′ ) + B(c, c′′ ).

            The two sides agree. ∎

            13. Pfaffian/orientation theorem
            Now make the Dirac/Pfaffian part precise.
            For a compact Calabi–Yau threefold X , Joyce–Upmeier prove natural orientation data
            for moduli stacks of coherent sheaves and perfect complexes; in their formulation,
            orientation data is a square root of the natural canonical-type line bundle compatible
            with short exact sequences. Since K3 × E is a compact Calabi–Yau threefold, this
            gives the correct general existence input for an unreduced CY3 sheaf/perfect-complex
            orientation datum. arXiv
            The Borisov–Joyce and Oh–Thomas theories are closely related Pfaffian/orientation
            technologies in the CY4 setting: Borisov–Joyce construct virtual classes for proper
            oriented (−2)-shifted symplectic derived schemes, and Oh–Thomas construct
            algebraic CY4 virtual cycles using localized square-root Euler classes. These are
            important analogues of the square-root/Pfaffian mechanism, but they do not by
            themselves prove the reduced K3 × E Hall orientation monodromy. arXiv +1

            29. Proof-hygiene fixes
            29.1 Avoid proof sketches where theorem is strong
            If a result says “vanishes,” give a proof. If proof is incomplete, call it a criterion or
            conjecture.
            29.2 Separate algebraic proof from geometric assumption
            For example:
                algebraic: B is a cocycle.
                geometric: Hall bracket realizes B -shift by Θ.
            Do not put both under one theorem unless assumptions are explicit.
            29.3 Do not use “standard” for nonstandard composites
https://chatgpt.com/c/69efa55c-63c4-83ea-b3fc-fc3666b5910f                                                                                              116/220
28/04/2026, 09:03                                            Attack Whitepaper Analysis

            “Standard equivariant Serre spectral sequence” is fine.
            “Standard equivariant derived setting of reduced K3 × E Hall stack with cosection and
            orientation descent” is not standard.
            29.4 Reduce citation stacking
            Several paragraphs list many orientation references. Instead:
                one paragraph says what exists in known CY3/CY4 literature,
                next paragraph says what is not covered here.
            29.5 Check dimensional language
            Replace every “fourfold” reference to K3 × E with “threefold.”

            30. Physics-strength upgrades
            30.1 Add a “Dirac principle” section
            Suggested statement:
               A scalar square is not square-rooted by choosing a branch. It is square-rooted by
               finding a first-order object with extra algebraic degrees of freedom. In this paper
               those degrees of freedom are orientation, primitive bracket, and normal-ordered
               charge descent.
            30.2 Add “unitarity before index, not after”
            The draft already says this. Make it a boxed principle:
             unitarity proves localization; the localized object is cohomological and virtual.                ​




            30.3 Add “states vs observables”
                    BPS states are superselection sectors. The local/factorization object is the algebra of
                    protected operations on sectors.
            30.4 Add “wrapped sectors are line defects over E ”
            A positive elliptic-degree brane should be physically compared to a wrapped/global
            operator, not a point insertion on E .

            31.4 Turn Θ-descent into a theorem about functors
            At chain level:
                                          Θc,c′ : Pc+c′ [Π(c + c′ )] → Pc+c′ [Π(c) + Π(c′ )]
                                                     ​           ​                                          ​




            with coherence:
                                                         Θc+c′ ,c′′ ∘ Θc,c′ = Θc,c′ +c′′ ∘ Θc′ ,c′′ .

            The equality is equivalent to δB = 0.

                                                           2        2     2

https://chatgpt.com/c/69efa55c-63c4-83ea-b3fc-fc3666b5910f                                                                                                           186/220
28/04/2026, 09:03                                                        Attack Whitepaper Analysis

            Your anatomy is the right research program, but the wording must be disciplined:
                                        The normal-ordered lattice theorem is proved.                         ​




                                                   The raw-descent no-go is proved.                   ​




                                         The Maass-side character theorem is proved.                      ​




             The Frobenius and cyclic routes are proved under precise CY3/cyclic hypotheses.                               ​




                      The compact Dirac–Igusa object is still the construction problem.                           ​




            The platonic clean paper is not one that pretends the compact host has been built. It is
            one that gives the exact finite-stage object to build, the exact obstruction classes to
            kill, the exact normal-ordered mechanism forced by the BKM bracket, and the exact
            theorem that would follow once the finite Hall–Dirac atlases, orientation package,
            hybrid wrapped source, Koszul source coalgebra, and primitive recognition data are
            constructed.

            1. Physical charge lattice

            even dyonic Mukai lattice.

            with Mukai pairing
                                             (r, D, s) ⋅ (r′ , D′ , s′ ) = D ⋅ D′ − rs′ − r′ s.

            12. Normal-ordered pushforward

                                                         [(PRΠ )γ , (PRΠ )γ ′ ] ⊆ (PRΠ )γ+γ ′ .

            13. How NO1–NO7 vanish in the constructed source
            The source-built normal-ordering kills the obstruction package as follows.
            NO1: finite-fibre descent
            At finite R, ΓX,R is finite. Therefore every fibre
                                      ​




                                                                   Π−1
                                                                    X (γ) ∩ ΓX,R​                       ​




            is finite.
            So ΠΘR,∗ is finite.
                         ​




            NO2: Hochschild boundary
            By construction,
                                                                 dHoch ΘΠ,R = Bch,R .
                                                                        ​               ​                       ​




            NO3: triple pentagon
            Associativity of ⋆ is equivalent to
                                          B(a, b) + B(a + b, c) = B(b, c) + B(a, b + c).

            Thus the degree pentagon is strict.

https://chatgpt.com/c/69efa55c-63c4-83ea-b3fc-fc3666b5910f                                                                      205/220
28/04/2026, 09:03                                                                    Attack Whitepaper Analysis

            The geometric pentagon is the equality of pull-push maps over the eight finite two-step
            flag stacks.
            NO4: Jacobi
            The Hall product is associative over finite two-step flags. Therefore its supercommutator
            satisfies Jacobi after passing to primitives.
            NO5: Frobenius
            The CY3 Serre pairing gives
                                                   ⟨[x, y], z⟩ + (−1)∣x∣∣y∣ ⟨y, [x, z]⟩ = 0.

            This is the Frobenius obstruction
                                                                         oF = 0.
                                                                             ​




            It follows once the protected category is cyclic Calabi–Yau of dimension 3, the primitive
            bracket is represented by the antisymmetrized Hall product, and the trace/pairing
            commute with finite R-transitions.
            NO6: negative cyclic lift
            The S 1-equivariant cyclic enhancement requires
                                                             (b + uBC )Θ−      −
                                                                        Π,R = Bch,R .
                                                                         ​                    ​               ​   ​




            The Loday–Quillen–Tsygan comparison gives the Hochschild shadow after forgetting
            the S 1-structure.
            NO7: radical stability
            Let
                                                                         RadR             ​




            be the radical of the completed Hopf pairing. Require
                                                              [RadR , PR ] ⊆ RadR ,
                                                                     ​               ​                ​




            and
                                              ΔR (RadR ) ⊆ RadR ⊗PR + PR ⊗ RadR .
                                                    ​          ​                 ​                ​       ​           ​




            Then the radical quotient remains a Lie bialgebra/Hopf primitive object.
https://chatgpt.com/c/69efa55c-63c4-83ea-b3fc-fc3666b5910f                                                                206/220
28/04/2026, 09:03                                                                                             Attack Whitepaper Analysis

            20. New content to add to the manuscript
            The work we just did clarifies several new insertions.
            20.1 Source-built normal ordering
            Add a definition:
               The normal-ordered Hall source is not a raw Γphys X -graded Hall object plus a later
               correction. It is a ΓX -graded Hall object whose product lands in c ⋆ c′ . Thus the
                                                                                                                                 ​




               correction B(c, c′ ) is part of the target label of the extension stack.
                                                    ​




            This eliminates the impression that ΘΠ is an arbitrary shift.                 ​

                                λ(A) = det RpE,∗ A ⊗ OE (−χ(A) ⋅ 0E ) ∈ Pic0 (E ) ≅ E.

            This gives a tangible rigidification for wrapped sectors.

            The most important new realization is:
             Normal-ordering is not a post-processing correction. It is the finite-stage degree law

            Once the source is ΓX -graded, the corrected Gram pushforward is functorial, the raw-

            category supplies the missing s-direction.
